Crest","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-title-7-565x377.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-1-565x377.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-2-565x330.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-3-565x486.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-4-565x377.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-5-565x377.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-11-565x342.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-7-565x376.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-8-565x353.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-9-565x269.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg","http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/10-graffiti-artists-that-make-our-world-a-better-place-10-565x305.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn0@2020_1/404.jpg"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598318106406},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:15:06","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:15:06","title":"Paul Brainard’s My Body is a Grave","link":"http://beautifuldecay.com/?p=153135","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-153140\" src=\"http://beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/Telephone_07-565x499.jpg\" alt=\"Telephone_07\" width=\"565\" height=\"499\" srcset=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/Telephone_07-565x499.jpg 565w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/Telephone_07-300x265.jpg 300w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/Telephone_07-768x678.jpg 768w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/Telephone_07-340x300.jpg 340w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 565px) 100vw, 565px\" /><br />\n<img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-153137\" src=\"http://beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/October-17-565x377.jpg\" alt=\"October 17\" width=\"565\" height=\"377\" srcset=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/October-17-565x377.jpg 565w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/October-17-184x124.jpg 184w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/October-17-300x200.jpg 300w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/October-17-768x512.jpg 768w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/October-17-450x300.jpg 450w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/October-17.jpg 1199w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 565px) 100vw, 565px\" /></p>\n<p>Walking up to the brick façade of an industrial NYC building, the rumble of a freight elevator vibrates through the entrance until it creeeeeaks to a halt on street level.  The gate lifts.  <a href=\"http://paulbrainard.com\">Paul Brainard</a> pushes one foot down onto the bottom half of the freight elevator door so I can climb inside.  Genial and quick, he leads me through a warren of artists’ studios, every space is spilling over with the alchemical instruments of the artist: tools, canvases, and paint.  Nestled against a large window is Paul’s studio with a drawing table and painting shelf.  After a few pleasantries, he reaches into a plywood painting rack and rotates with a golden frame that catches the evening light in a bloom of yellow.  The drawing inside is so thick with gunmetal tone graphite it hardly resembles paper.  Underneath glass, some images are suspended like intricate seahorses, in a thought-space, thick and transparent, like gelatin.  Other images appear to dance languidly on the metallic ground. Paul talks briefly, painfully, about how both his parents passed away this year.  He shows me a tattoo on his arm from an old New England gravestone rubbing.  Everything, the language, people in his life, and images in his drawings, are appearing and receding like a tide.  Paul addresses this topic we all eventually face with a solo show, <em>My body is a grave</em>, opening October 6<sup>th</sup> at the <a href=\"http://www.secondstreetgallery.org\">Second Street Gallery</a> in Charlottesville, Virginia.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153135\"></span></p>\n<p>I want to try and link Paul’s art to contemporaneous philosophy and art history.  Primarily through the writing of thoughtful people: the art historians Caroline Walker Bynum and Georges Didi-Huberman, the historian Charles Freeman, and the philosopher Martin Seel.  Let me begin with the philosopher Martin Seel, in his book <em>The Aesthetics of Appearing</em>, he describes three forms of appearing: mere appearing, atmospheric appearing, and artistic appearing.  Mere appearing is noticing an object through your sense of sight.  Atmospheric appearing is when you notice something through your sense of sight, but the object goes beyond mere appearing by being a catalyst for further thoughts and memories.  Artistic appearing is when an object is crafted in order to appear.  Seel writes: “Artworks differ in principle from other objects of appearing by virtue of their being <em>presentations</em>.” (95)</p>\n<p>Paul talks about his parents, and how they took him to see a Kiss concert when he was 8 and the film <em>Alien</em> when he was 10, and, at the same time, were Catholic.  His describes his parents as liberal Catholics who were fans of his art, and that despite Paul’s images being a bombardment of pornography and death, they were always interested in and proactive in responding to his work.  Paul’s father was a professor of chemical engineering, and would send Paul books about ecological and scientific crises.  There are three things which emerge from this brief family history: pop culture, religion, and warnings about the future.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-153136\" src=\"http://beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/mybodyisagrave-565x386.jpg\" alt=\"mybodyisagrave\" width=\"565\" height=\"386\" srcset=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/mybodyisagrave-565x386.jpg 565w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/mybodyisagrave-300x205.jpg 300w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/mybodyisagrave-768x525.jpg 768w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/mybodyisagrave-439x300.jpg 439w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 565px) 100vw, 565px\" /></p>\n<p>The largest drawing in the show shares the name of the exhibition, <em>My Body is a Grave</em>, and is rich with references to Paul’s oeuvre and art history.  Along the bottom of the drawing is a dual-corpse with a dead body <em>and</em> a semi-decomposed portrait beginning to sit up, apparently from the same person.  It is a self-portrait.  The left arm points towards a small old-fashioned photo of Paul’s father.  This type of double image dates back to the middle ages, and, in particular, this drawing reminds me of the <em>Transi Tomb of Henry Chichele.</em>  Chichele was a 15<sup>th</sup> century Archbishop of Canterbury who briefly appears in Shakespeare’s <em>Henry V</em>.  Panofsky called Chichele’s tomb a “double-decker tomb,” because it is two tombs.  The tomb has two reclining statues: below, a desiccated corpse; above, a resplendently clothed man with open eyes.  This type of art combines the physical decay of death, the rotting corpse, with the lasting effects of a person’s life, the resplendent robes signifying achievement and status.</p>\n<p>The top center of<em> My Body is a Grave </em>has the words Toten Uber Alles, which is German for ‘Death Above All.’  The <em>Transi Tomb</em> has this text written in the area between the two bodies:</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">“Pauper eram natus, post Primas hic elevates</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">Iam sum prostrates et vermibus esca paratus</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">Ecce meum tumulum.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">Quisquis eris qui transieris rogo memoreris</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">Tu quod eris mihi consimilis qui post morieris</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">Omnibus horribili, pulvis, vermis, caro vilis.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p>Above the head of the resplendently clothed Archbishop is the following inscription:</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">Etus sanctorum concorditer iste precetur</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">Ut Dues ipsorum meritis sibi propitietur.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p>This Latin inscription translates to “I was a pauper born, then to Primate raised/Now I am cut down and ready to be food for worms/Behold my grave./Whoever you may be who passes by, I ask you to remember/You will be like me after you die;/All horrible, dust, worms, vile flesh.”  The inscription above the head translates to: “May this gathering of the saints pray in harmony/That God may be propitious towards their merits.”  The Latin comes from this source: Kathleen Cohen, <em>Metamorphosis of a Death Symbol: The Transi Tomb in the Late Middle Ages and the Renaissance</em>, (Berkeley: University of California Press, 1973) 15-16.</p>\n<p>In Paul’s drawing, the double body is surrounded by skulls, one skeleton, three nude women, a dog, Rudy Giuliani, the ‘see something say something’ NYC subway ad guy, the photograph of Paul’s deceased father, and a child – and the corpse comes back to life.  If we are dealing with medieval Christian art, like the <em>Transi Tomb</em>, then this relates to the sacredness of the body.  If we are dealing with 21<sup>st</sup> century pop culture, then this body is a zombie bombarded by our chaotic culture.  A zombie is a monster that refuses to die, and who eats brains – the ability to think; essentially the opposite of a graceful passing.  Paul addresses this type of collapsing symbolic structure on his website, writing “Time is compressed; forms overlap and eradicate one another.”</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-153141\" src=\"http://beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/thesouthwillriseagain-565x715.jpg\" alt=\"thesouthwillriseagain\" width=\"565\" height=\"715\" srcset=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/thesouthwillriseagain-565x715.jpg 565w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/thesouthwillriseagain-237x300.jpg 237w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/thesouthwillriseagain.jpg 759w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 565px) 100vw, 565px\" /></p>\n<p>Here is a weird etymological coincidence.  I learned about this through the art historian Georges Didi-Huberman.  1. Paul’s father sent him books warning about ecological disaster.  2. Paul’s work is full of bodies that can easily flip between religious symbols and pop culture monsters. Latin for ‘to warn’ is moneo.  Moneo is listed in some sources as the origin of the latin words monstrum and monstrare.  Monstrum means both omen and monster.  Monstrare means to show.  Monstrance, a modernization of monstrare, is the word Catholics use for the sculpture that holds the Eucharist or a relic – to display the sacred body.  The words which means to warn, to show, and monster are linked in ancient language.  Can it be a coincidence that these three themes populate Paul Brainard’s work?</p>\n<p>In the beginning of this essay I told you I would link Paul’s work to contemporary philosophy and art history, and, to that end, presented Martin Seel’s definition of artistic appearing – something crafted as a presentation.  Seel’s definition is potentially the driest definition of art in existence.  Looking briefly at Paul’s family and work, we found an etymological coincidence, linking these four concepts: showing, omens, warnings, and monsters.  Paul talks about collapsing symbolic structure, and if you collapse showing, omens, warnings, and monsters – you get an idea very close to Seel’s idea of artistic appearing.</p>\n<p>Let’s flesh this out a little.  If a zombie is a permanently rotting body, essentially similar to the art historical transi sculpture, and we also recognize that within the same image we can have the sacred representation of life, then we are walking into a debate that is hundreds of years old and is still intellectually raging today.  The sacred body enters in academic culture through philosophers like Giorgio Amgaben’s <em>Homo Sacer</em>, and into moral political culture through Ta-Nehisi Coates’ <em>Between the World and Me.</em> If we keep in mind both the profane rotting corpse and the sacred memory of life, we can learn something from art history.  Caroline Walker Bynum, an art historian at Princeton, wrote this about 15<sup>th</sup> century British transi tombs: “In contrast to the reliquaries, which both sublimate and reveal the object within, unveiling its decay-resistance as bone or wood yet lifting it to immortal life through gold or crystal, other medieval sculpture is obsessed with displaying not just death but also the decay that reliquaries resist.  This quite common motif of the <em>transi</em> tomb (a sculpture which is decaying, worm-eaten corpse lies beneath a gorgeously clothed member of the elite, represented more as sleeping than as dead) uses the stone from which it is carved to image slimy, percolating flesh…  (As opposed to reliquaries)…the lower part of the <em>transi</em> tomb are almost always naked stone; it is as if the transformation works the other way.  Putrefaction is not just imaged; it is not just emphasized; it is made permanent.  In the <em>transi</em> tomb, it is the clothes above (elegant and ordered) that deny decay, but below, the body seems (oxymoronically) frozen in its character as decayable and decaying.” Caroline Walker Bynum, <em>Christian Materiality: As Essay on Religion in Late Medieval Europe</em>, (New York: Zone Book, 2011) 71-79.</p>\n<p>Paul is frank about his politics, and voices his support for progressive policies and causes.  The politicization of the body is at least as old as the Medieval period, and we can find a related historical example in the historian Charles Freeman’s fantastic and entertaining book <em>Holy Bones, Holy Dust</em>:  In 1247, roughly one hundred and fifty years before Henry Chichele first rose to power in England, the King of England, Henry III, saw himself as gaining status and power via a blood cult.  The blood cult centered around a reliquary containing Christ’s blood which came from Jerusalem.  The Bishop of Norwich declared, regarding the distinction England earned via owning the blood of Christ while France only had the Cross: “Now it is true that the Cross is a very holy relic but it is holy only because it came into direct contact with the precious blood of Christ.  The holiness of the Cross derives from the blood whereas the holiness of the blood in no way derives from the Cross.  It therefore follows that England, which possesses the blood of Christ, rejoices in a greater treasure than France, which has no more than the Cross.” [1] Charles Freeman, <em>Holy Bones, Holy Dust: How Relics Shaped the History of Medieval Europe</em>, (New Haven: Yale University Press, 2011) 188-189.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-153146\" src=\"http://beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/The-Battle-for-Bedford-Ave-1-565x377.jpg\" alt=\"The Battle for Bedford Ave\" width=\"565\" height=\"377\" srcset=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/The-Battle-for-Bedford-Ave-1-565x377.jpg 565w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/The-Battle-for-Bedford-Ave-1-184x124.jpg 184w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/The-Battle-for-Bedford-Ave-1-300x200.jpg 300w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/The-Battle-for-Bedford-Ave-1-768x512.jpg 768w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/The-Battle-for-Bedford-Ave-1-450x300.jpg 450w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 565px) 100vw, 565px\" /></p>\n<p>In the drawing <em>The Battle for Bedford Ave </em>Paul Brainard enters into less personal territory, and addresses NYC and pop culture.  Bearded Confederate generals mix with bearded hipsters, and the fictional MKULTRA type character – Jason Bourne, intermixes with Osama bin Laden, Iron Maiden’s power ballad zombie, and supermodels. In an interview for the show with Eric White, Paul expressed his beliefs about art and politics: “There is a certain reactionary atmosphere that surrounds current discourse in contemporary art that is very stifling and not very nuanced in the understanding that most artists are on the same side (and that this side is the side of liberal progressives).  In general, I have found most artists are liberals or libertarians, opposed to racial, gender and sexual oppression.   But you would never know this in the contemporary discourse surrounding contemporary art.”</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-153144\" src=\"http://beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0110-565x424.jpg\" alt=\"IMG_0110\" width=\"565\" height=\"424\" srcset=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0110-565x424.jpg 565w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0110-300x225.jpg 300w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0110-768x576.jpg 768w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0110-400x300.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 565px) 100vw, 565px\" /></p>\n<p>Paul is also an accomplished oil painter, and makes compositions that have deep perspectival space – that at the same time is disjointed. The paintings have a feeling of rapid movement that is chopped into discrete moments.  At the same time, a recurrent image is a flat wall with double doors, like a subway car.  The paintings imply movement, stoppage, and passage.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-153143\" src=\"http://beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0111-565x424.jpg\" alt=\"IMG_0111\" width=\"565\" height=\"424\" srcset=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0111-565x424.jpg 565w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0111-300x225.jpg 300w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0111-768x576.jpg 768w, http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/IMG_0111-400x300.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 565px) 100vw, 565px\" /></p>\n<p>This essay will finish with Paul’s oil painting <em>Necros.</em>  Necros is the name of Mid-Western punk band whose most famous album was <em>Conquest for Death.</em>  Necros is also very close to the word necropsy, which is another term for autopsy.  The middle of the painting is filled with zooming diagonal spaces which set up a three-dimensional sense of depth.  Foregrounded is a self-portrait of Paul in zombie makeup, and the words “Horror!!! your host Swamp Honkey.”</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/2017/10/05/paul-brainards-body-grave/\">Paul Brainard&#8217;s My Body is a Grave</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" announced and we couldn’t be more excited! The global design award was established to create awareness for groundbreaking design in a wide array of genres. The ultimate aim of the A’ Design Award &#38; Competition is to build strong incentives for designers, companies and brands from all countries to come up with better products, services and systems that benefit mankind.</p>\n<p>This years winners included some of the most talented creatives from around the planet. class=\"wp-caption-text\">Interior Design: Le Campus</p></div>\n<p>International design competition <a href=\"http://www.whatisadesignaward.com\">A&#8217; Design Awards</a> provides creatives a unique opportunity to their artwork on a global stage. Not only do designers get recognition by their peers but  it also works as a powerful marketing campaign for the winners brand. Some categories that creatives can apply to compete in include  <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-industrial-design.html\" target=\"_blank\">Good Industrial Design Award</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-architecture-design.html\" target=\"_blank\">Good Architecture Design Award</a>,  <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-product-design.html\" target=\"_blank\">Good Product Design Award</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-communication-design.html\" target=\"_blank\">Good Communication Design Award</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-service-design.html\" target=\"_blank\">Good Service Design Award</a>,  and <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-fashion-design.html\" target=\"_blank\">Good Fashion Design Award</a>. Entries will be judged by an international jury panel of academics, design professionals and press members who will look for groundbreaking design, innovation and out of the box thinking.  The deadline to register and submit your work is February 28th so make sure to apply today. You can do so <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">here</a>. Winning designs will be announced on the A&#8217; Design Awards website and on Beautiful/Decay on April 15th. Yeung</p></div>\n<p>I may not be a design guru, but I think I put together a pretty outstanding group of past A&#8217; Design winners. What do you think?</p>\n<p>Does your work fit in with past winners and <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/\">A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition</a> panelists’ favorite projects?</p>\n<p>As I browsed through the extensive list of winners, I realized that exceptional design expands to not only visual arts and commercial packaging, but also furniture, architecture, fashion and more; that’s why it’s so important to recognize A’ Design as inclusive and influential.</p>\n<p>A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition recognizes the best and most exciting work in design with big prizes and benefits. Awards include perks such as participation in an international exhibition, inclusion in annual hardcover yearbook, a press release, publicity through the Competition’s extensive network, inclusion in the World Design Rankings, an invitation to a gala-night event in Italy for a unique networking opportunity, an award trophy and certificate, translation services for your press release into more than 20 languages, feedback notes from the jurors, a Designer of the Year nomination, sales listing for winning designs and much more. If that’s not enough, you can count on your work getting tons of attention; the winning designs will have tons of exposure. On average, A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition winners’ website has 24,404,321 impressions on average per competition cycle.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153340\"></span></p>\n<p>As if that’s not enough, entries to the Competition are judged by an international jury panel of scholars, industry experts, and prominent journalists. Unlike many other awards, the A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition follows a strict methodology including a peer-review process with anonymous voting.</p>\n<p>As mentioned prior, A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition rewards designers in varying categories, therefore submissions are accepted in dozens of categories ensuring that your work finds its best fit. This includes categories such as <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-industrial-design.html\">Good Industrial Design</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-architecture-design.html\">Good Architecture Design</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-product-design.html\">Good Product Design</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-communication-design.html\">Good Communication Design</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-service-design.html\">Good Service Design</a>, and<a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-fashion-design.html\"> Good Fashion Design</a>. You can find further design categories <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-fashion-design.html\">here</a>. <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/entryinstructions.html\">Entry instructions</a> are also easy!</p>\n<p>You can learn everything you need to know about the competition at designaward.com. The deadline for submissions is February 28th, 2019. You can register by clicking <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">here</a>.</p>\n<div id=\"attachment_153345\" style=\"width: 575px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img class=\"wp-caption-text\">MU&#8217;trans Home Accessories, MU&#8217;factory Cetti Davi and Dario Feo, Italy</p></div>\n<p>How does your country stack up? The World Design Ranking (WDR) ranks nations  around the world based on the number of creative designers that have received an A’ Design Award over the course of the past seven years. Envisioned to be to design what the Olympics are to sports, the A’ Design Award &#38; Competition aims stoke innovation and the flexing of minds through international competition through the WDR. (You can find the full world ranking and each nation’s awardees at <a href=\"http://www.worlddesignrankings.com/\">http://www.worlddesignrankings.com</a>.)</p>\n<p>Amazing and forward-thinking designs are submitted globally to the A’ Design Award &#38; Competition each year keeping the rankings close and the list of represented nations long. There’s still time to represent your home and add to your country’s award total. The A’ Design Award &#38; Competition registration period is now open and accepting submissions for numerous categories including packaging design; architecture, building and structure design; arts, crafts and ready-made design among many more. You can register and find out more <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">here</a>. In the meantime, check out selection of awarded submissions by designers from the top 10 nations on the WDR.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153154\"></span></p>\n<div id=\"attachment_153163\" style=\"width: class=\"wp-caption-text\">Heaven is a Place on Earth Swarovski Veil by reginadahmeningenhoven</p></div>\n<p>With a highly respected and influential panel of judges and an award that offers international audiences and recognition, the <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/\" target=\"_blank\">A’ Design Award &#38; Competition</a> is one of the world’s leading annual juried competitions for design. While design-lovers would be interested in perusing past years’ winners, artists and designers should know: the application period is now open.</p>\n<p>The sought after “A’ Design Prize” entails an extensive winners kit including a certificate, a trophy, inclusion in a hardcover yearbook publication and much more, culminating in invitations to an exclusive gala-night in Italy. Winners also receive vital tools for international promotion and marketing such as project translation into more than 20 languages, media appearances through the press partners of A’ Design Award &#38; Competition as well as press release preparation and distribution.</p>\n<p>Each year, submissions are judged and winners are ultimately selected by a panel of leading designers, academics, entrepreneurs and prominent members of the press. This diverse group of panelists are selected from a variety of fields for their recognition and, more importantly, their experience and technical knowledge. To ensure fair evaluation, the basis for any proper design competition, the panelists abide by a conflict of interest policy and a jury agreement and judge the submissions anonymously using a rigorous methodology.</p>\n<p>Does your work fit in with past winners and panelists’ favorite projects? I may not be a panelist (or even describe myself as “esteemed”), but enjoyed picking 20 winners from past years that especially caught my eye. When the results from this year&#8217;s competition are made public, we&#8217;ll feature a selection of our favorites once again. Enjoy the collection and best wishes!</p>\n<p>The <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/call-for-entries.html\" target=\"_blank\">call to entries</a> is now open. Find out more information and register <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\" target=\"_blank\">here</a>.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153066\"></span></p>\n<div Quebra-Pedra 3D puzzle by Priscila Busato &#8211; (Brazil)</p></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400; color: #000000;\">It has been an incredible year in terms of art and design. Throughout 2018, we’ve been sharing several of our favorite designers who have won the A&#8217; Design Award and we simply cannot end the year without sharing some more&#8230;and something extra. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #000000;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/theaward.html\">A’ Design Award and Competition</a> is the world’s most inclusive and largest design competition that rewards creatives with highly sought-after prizes, industry insights, and feedback. It is because of it’s incredible perks that many creatives around the world enter to win. This means that the A’ Design Award and Competition has gathered </span>incisive <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">data on the world’s best and brightest of design.</span></span></p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153363\"></span></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #000000;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"http://www.worlddesignrankings.com/#rankings\">World Design Rankings</a>, aka WDR, is informed by design applicants and ranks all the countries based on the number of designers that have been granted with the award. WDR is to design what the Olympics is to sports. The sole purpose of sharing this data is to incentivize&#8230;can you spot your country in the ranking? Did your country make it to the top 10? </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A’ Design Award and Competition</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> wants to push countries to compete with their designers’  innovative ideas and brain muscles.</span></span></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://www.worlddesignrankings.com/#rankings\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-153376 aligncenter\" src=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/2018-24-12-WorldDesignRankings.fw_-1-252x900.png\" alt=\"2018-24-12-WorldDesignRankings.fw\" width=\"338\" height=\"1172\" /></a></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #000000;\">Check out some of the best of 2018 in this post!</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"color: #000000;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Do you have what it takes? If you’re a designer (of any kind), there is a category in the competition for you. The full list includes 100 different categories such as </span><span style=\"color: #0000ff;\"><a style=\"color: #0000ff;\" href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-industrial-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Industrial Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, </span><a style=\"color: #0000ff;\" href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-architecture-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Architecture Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, </span><a style=\"color: #0000ff;\" href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-product-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Product Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, </span><a style=\"color: #0000ff;\" href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-communication-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Communication Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, </span><a style=\"color: #0000ff;\" href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-service-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Service Design </span></a>and <a style=\"color: #0000ff;\" href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-fashion-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Fashion Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <span style=\"color: #000000;\">You can find more design categories </span></span><span style=\"color: #000000;\"><a style=\"color: #000000;\" href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/categories.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">here</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></span></span></span></p>\n<p><span winners and <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/\">A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition</a> panelists’ favorite projects? I may not be a design rockstar, but I enjoyed putting together a group of 20 winners from past years that made an impact on me.</p>\n<p>As I browsed through the winners, I  deduced that good design expands to not only visual arts and commercial packaging, but also furniture, architecture, fashion and more; that’s why it’s so important to recognize A’ Design as an inclusive and influential competition. We are excited to announce that one of the most inclusive design competitions in the world of design is accepting entries.</p>\n<p>It is the reward of beauty and innovation that keeps designers producing the very best…except that sometimes it isn’t. That’s why A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition recognizes the best and most exciting work in design with big prizes and benefits. Awards include perks such as participation in an international exhibition, inclusion in annual hardcover yearbook, a press release, publicity through the Competition’s extensive network, inclusion in the World Design Rankings, an invitation to a gala-night event in Italy for a unique networking opportunity, an award trophy and certificate, translation services for your press release into more than 20 languages, feedback notes from the jurors, a Designer of the Year nomination, sales listing for winning designs and much more. If that’s not enough, you can count on your work getting tons of attention; the winning designs will have tons of exposure. On average, A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition winners’ website has 24,404,321 impressions on average per competition cycle.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153275\"></span></p>\n<p>As if that’s not enough, entries to the Competition are judged by an international jury panel of scholars, industry experts, and prominent journalists. Unlike many other awards, the A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition follows a strict methodology including a peer-review process with anonymous voting.</p>\n<p>As mentioned prior, A’ Design Awards &#38; Competition rewards designers in varying categories, therefore submissions are accepted in dozens of categories ensuring that your work finds its best fit. This includes categories such as <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-industrial-design.html\">Good Industrial Design</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-architecture-design.html\">Good Architecture Design</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-product-design.html\">Good Product Design</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-communication-design.html\">Good Communication Design</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-service-design.html\">Good Service Design</a>, and<a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-fashion-design.html\"> Good Fashion Design</a>. You can find further design categories <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-fashion-design.html\">here</a>. <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/entryinstructions.html\">Entry instructions</a> are also easy!</p>\n<p>You can learn everything you need to know about the competition at designaward.com. The deadline for submissions is February 28th, 2019. You can register by clicking <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">here</a>.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-large wp-image-153287\" (detail) by Naai-Jung Shih</p></div>\n<p>As you may already know, the A’ Design Award &#38; Competition is a very large and one of the world’s leading design competitions. Judged by academics, prominent members of the press and successful professionals around the world, awarded designers are the minds behind frequently very compelling projects. Further, there are many categories (100 of them, in fact) covering just about every facet of modern design. Registration for the award is now open. You can find out more and register <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">here</a>.</p>\n<p>In the meantime, however, we take a look at past winners of one category: Arts, Crafts and Ready-Made design. This category encompasses works of art, crafted designs and ready-made objects as well as installations and functional sculptures. The Arts, Crafts and Ready-Made Design category would be of particular interest to professional and young artists, designers, design galleries, design and arts departments, and other art, craft and design oriented institutions in the creative industry around the world and all are encouraged to submit.</p>\n<p>In addition to a trophy, invitation to a gala celebration in Italy and numerous other perks of a lengthy prize package list, award winners are also offered the opportunity to exhibit their work, a free service, and make their work available for purchase free of any commission. You can find the full award package and more information on the A’ Design Award &#38; Competition at <a href=\"http://www.designaward.com/\">http://www.designaward.com</a>.</p>\n<p>Can your art, craft or ready-made design hold its own against these past winners? If so consider registering now <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">here</a>.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153111\"></span></p>\n<div id=\"attachment_153119\" style=\"width: <a href=\"https://booking.design/\">booking.design</a>.</p>\n<p>The .design extension functions in the same way a .com or .net does. However, anyone that has ever registered a domain knows that the short and good .com domains were snatched up decades ago. So, instead of settling for a clunky name, you can now stick out with something both elegant and innovative. You can often shorten or improve your existing branding by switching to .design; you can set up a fun coordinating email address (holler@yourname.design); or you can even use it as a clever redirect to another site, like a behance profile.</p>\n<p>.design is being used across the varied design disciplines and so it is creating a growing and diffuse online community of creatives. UX and web designers are the fastest adopters but there is really strong representation of more niche fields like lighting design as well.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://we.design/?coupon=BEAUTIFUL\">We.design</a> is now offering $5 .design names to Beautiful/Decay readers, and every domain comes with free WHOIS privacy as well as SSL certificates. width=\"565\" height=\"565\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><br />\nAs an arts blogger I spend most of my day looking at amazing things created by artists, performers and creatives. If you’re reading </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Beautiful/Decay</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, a good portion of your time is likely also spent in awe of the creative output of others. I decided to make a move to the other side of the screen, rolled up my sleeves and learned to create something awesome. I joined forces with </span><a href=\"http://skl.sh/bdhome\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Skillshare</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, an online learning community that provides access to over 15,000 creative classes, to help accelerate my creative inspiration. Whether you’re looking to learn graphic design, illustration, photography or practically anything else, Skillshare can teach you what you need to know to execute your vision. Even better, they’re offering </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Beautiful/Decay</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> readers two free months of Skillshare Premium (usually it’s $10 per month). Visit this </span><a href=\"http://skl.sh/bdpromo1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">link to redeem the promo</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> or use the promo code BEAUTIFULDECAY..</span></p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153039\"></span></p>\n<p><iframe style=\"border: none; overflow: hidden;\" src=\"https://www.facebook.com/plugins/video.php?href=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.facebook.com%2Fskillshare%2Fvideos%2F1787060051319423%2F&#38;show_text=0&#38;width=400\" width=\"565\" height=\"565\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> I decided to take Skillshare Premium for a test drive with designer Aaron Draplin’s new class “</span><a href=\"http://skl.sh/bddraplin\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Customizing Type with Draplin</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">” and very quickly it became clear I was in for a fast, fun and, at times, very funny class.</span></p>\n<p>Draplin began by “Junkin’ for References”—hitting shops around Portland, Oregon in search of inspiration, ideas, and cool vintage letterform. This brief video has had me really looking at the design I run into everyday in a new light and the overall class showed me ideas about letterform and text design that can’t be unseen.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Immediately, Draplin works to “get you away from the default,” as he puts it. That is, to not accept a font as it’s handed to you, but to chop it up, stretch it and generally do whatever it takes to create the unique design you need and want. He primarily works in Adobe Illustrator throughout the class and prefers continuously creating something to overthinking it, so it was helpful watching Draplin’s videos on one screen while having Illustrator open on another.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There were (more than a few) instances during the class I literally yelled “Yes!” at my screen as if cheering on good text design. Draplin covered fundamentals such as kerning, tracking and letterform, which was extremely helpful for someone like me, with a background in visual art but none in design. However, especially if you’re new to creating wordmarks, it’s his quick tricks, ideas and keyboard shortcuts that will also have you also cheering through your screen. </span></p>\n<p><iframe style=\"border: none; overflow: hidden;\" src=\"https://www.facebook.com/plugins/video.php?href=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.facebook.com%2Fskillshare%2Fvideos%2F1798680616824033%2F&#38;show_text=0&#38;width=400\" width=\"565\" height=\"565\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the seventh video lesson, we got off the computer and back to the classics of pen and paper. Other lessons showed me how to lift those designs off my journal pages and back onto the computer, how to add texture to fonts and how to prepare designs for the real world on t-shirts, patches, coin purses.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If there is something you are excited about, you can inspire that same excitement in others through good design. This is the thought that is essentially behind Draplin’s personality and philosophy. It’s what made his video so enjoyable, encouraging me to create with an open mind instead of the usual self-deprecating stress. The large collection of student projects show that the message got through as students around the world create and share designs on par with the instructor. I’m looking forward to adding mine to the bunch. If you’re itching to go on your own creative journey, try two months of Skillshare Premium </span><a href=\"http://skl.sh/bdpromo2\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">for free here</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, learn everything you need know (and some things you didn’t) and add your project to the gallery.</span></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"http://www.beautifuldecay.com/2017/05/16/learn-customize-type-aaron-draplin/\">Learn to Customize Type With Aaron Draplin</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" Lifi by Edmundas Jankauskas</p></div>\n<p><em>Above, images of past design winners. </em></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A n</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">ew year, a new award. Your career deserves a boost! So why not take advantage of a new entry date for A’ Design Award and Competition?</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you’re a designer (of any kind), and you think you deserve it, there is a category in the competition for you. The full list includes 100 different categories such as </span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-industrial-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Industrial Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, </span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-architecture-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Architecture Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, </span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-product-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Product Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, </span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-communication-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Communication Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, </span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-service-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Service Design </span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">and </span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-fashion-design.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Good Fashion Design</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. You can find more design categories </span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/categories.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">here</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The A’ Design Award and Competition is the world’s most inclusive and largest design competition that rewards creatives with highly sought-after prizes and industry insights and feedback. It aims to highlight the best designs, concepts and design-oriented products around the globe each year. The deadline for new submission is F</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">ebruary 28, 2019</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Nominate your designs for award consideration </span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">here</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span id=\"more-153381\"></span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Entries will be judged by an international jury panel of academics, design professionals, and press members using fair evaluation and an extensive methodology.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The comprehensive A’ Design Award Winners Kit is, of course, one of the main reason many register and compete in the A’ Design Award and Competition. Just some of the benefits this award package includes are: participation in an exhibition at the Museum of Outstanding Design (MOOD), inclusion in an annual hardcover yearbook, publicity by way of tools such as a press release and marketing, inclusion in the World Design Rankings, an invitation to the A’ Design Award Gala-Night in Como, Italy, an award trophy (</span><a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/trophy-images.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">check it out</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">), feedback notes from the jury, press release translation into more than 20 languages, the Prime Design Mark, and participation in a extensive PR campaign. However, many say that the feedback from experienced professionals alone is the most valuable prize. This strong jury brings knowledge and insight to each category, evaluating them expertly and providing valuable feedback experience from a panel of from industry leaders, academics and prestigious journalists.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The deadline for submission is F</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">ebruary 28</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The winners will be released to the public on April 15th, 2019.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You can learn more about the A’ Design Award and Competition at </span><a href=\"http://www.designaward.com/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">designaward.com</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><em>Below, some more images of past design Toilet Paper by Kazuaki Kawahara</p></div>\n<div>With the motto &#8220;Ars Futura Cultura&#8221; i.e. Arts Cultivate the Future, Arts for the Culture of Future, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">A’ Design Award</a> was created as a platform to highlight, advertise and advocate groundbreaking design and designers A’ Design Award. Their yearly award attracts aglobal audience of creatives from all design related fields who compete for the top slot. More than just an award A’ Design Award is recognized worldwide as a certificate of Excellence and proof of quality, invention, and out of the box thinking. Nominate your design <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">Here</a>.</div>\n<div><span id=\"more-152965\"></span></div>\n<div></div>\n<div>The competition has many categories allowing for a wide definition of design to be featured. Creatives can compete in such categories as  <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-industrial-design.html\">Good Industrial Design Award</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-architecture-design.html\">Good Architecture Design Award</a>, <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-product-design.html\">Good Product Design Award</a>,  <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-communication-design.html\">Good Communication Design Award</a>,  <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-service-design.html\">Good Service Design Award</a>,  <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/good-fashion-design.html\">Good Fashion Design Award</a> and more. For a full listing of categories click <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/categories.html\">here</a>.</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>The deadline for submissions is coming up fast at February 28th.  Entries will be judged by an international jury panel of scholars, professionals and media members who will be looking for innovation, creativity, skill, and original problem solving. Winners of the awards will be announced April 15th both on Beautiful/Decay as well as on  the <a href=\"https://competition.adesignaward.com/registration.php\">A’ Design Award website</a>. Learn more about the competion <a href=\"http://www.whatisadesignaward.com/\">here</a> and apply today and share your creativity with the world.</div>\n<div></div>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<div
